Sun Ke Discusses the Course of the Lushan Conference 87

The Japanese Army's Coercion and the Treacherous Activities of Traitors Forced a Ceasefire

It Was Agreed That Politics Would Not Be Involved and That Military Authorities Would Preside

With the Rise of Feng's Army, Japan Used It as an Excuse to Attack Chahar, Creating a Critical Situation

Sun Ke, President of the Legislative Yuan, arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning from Nanjing, accompanied by Legislative Committee Member Ma Chaojun, Secretary Lü Guang, and others, to visit his mother and to discuss the draft constitution with Constitution Drafting Committee Member Wu Jingxiong and others. Mr. Sun received reporters from various newspapers at his private residence on Columbia Road at 10:00 AM yesterday morning. The main points of his discussion are as follows:

(Lushan Conference) Mr. Sun first stated that the gathering of key Central figures in Lushan this time was not a formal meeting but merely a discussion to exchange ideas. All important issues were discussed, including the ceasefire agreement, the suppression of communists, the Southwest problem, Mr. Feng's affairs, and the National People's Congress. The ceasefire agreement was based entirely on military principles, with no mention of any political or diplomatic issues. Regarding the Southwest and Mr. Feng's affairs, it was planned to send people to explain the situation. The provisional National People's Congress was changed to a formal meeting on November 12th.

(Ceasefire Process) Regarding the process of signing the ceasefire agreement in North China this time, after the Japanese army occupied the area south of the Great Wall and coerced Tianjin and Beiping, our side was in a military impasse because the Great Wall line had completely fallen and Nantianmen was also lost. At the same time, the Japanese side presented a memorandum to us, stating that if the ceasefire agreement was not accepted, the Japanese army would attack Beiping and Tianjin. Under these circumstances, the Central Government painfully negotiated a ceasefire with the Japanese side. Huang Fu, Chairman of the Political Affairs Committee, consulted with He Yingqin, Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission, and jointly telegraphed the Central Government for instructions. After the Central Government considered the results, the following principles were decided: (1) The agreement would be limited to oral agreements and would not be written. (2) No buffer zones would be established. (3) It would be limited to military affairs and would not include political affairs. (4) The meeting would be handled solely by military authorities on both sides, with no participation from diplomatic or political officials. As a result, the Japanese side did not agree to points two and three, but our side, needing to deal with both resistance to Japan and traitors, had no choice but to amend and sign the existing agreement, excluding any political issues, to the Japanese memorandum. As for the rumors of recognizing "Manchukuo," that is definitely not the case. The matter of creating "Manchukuo" relates to the entire change in the international situation, and not only is it absolutely impossible for our country to recognize it, but it is also impossible for the international community to recognize it.

(Southwest Problem) Mr. Sun continued by saying that the comrades in the Southwest, as well as Jiang Guangnai, Cai Tingkai, and others, opposed the ceasefire in their telegrams, all because they did not understand the situation in North China. The Central Government has already telegraphed an explanation and should be able to understand the actual situation and appreciate the difficulties. The suppression of the communists by troops from the Southwest is also progressing. In short, everyone must understand the facts and cooperate to fight the communists and resist Japan in order to have a solution.

(Feng's Resistance Against Japan) The fighting in the Tianjin-Beiping area has now ended. A demilitarized zone has been established between the Chinese and Japanese armies, so there will be no conflict for the time being. However, since Mr. Feng Yuxiang has independently raised the banner of resistance against Japan, the Japanese side has paid considerable attention. The Japanese army along the Great Wall is now moving towards the northwest to concentrate, and is about to attack Chahar Province. Feng's army is also advancing south from Duolun, attempting to attack Zhangjiakou. The situation in Chahar Province is extremely critical. Mr. Feng only has 3,000 guards, and in addition, there are a small number of mixed troops, making their strength extremely weak. If the national army inside the pass sends reinforcements to Chahar Province, there is deep concern that it will cause Mr. Feng's misunderstanding, so it is difficult for the Central Government to send troops to assist. Huang Yingbai, chairman of the Beiping Political Affairs Reorganization Committee, has now dispatched representatives to meet with Feng in Chahar to discuss everything so that Chahar Province will not fall into the hands of the enemy.

(National Congress) At the time, everyone at the provisional National People's Congress believed that the North China incident was important and wanted to unite all comrades outside the party to save the situation together. Later, the Southwest misunderstood the nature of the congress and opposed it in a telegram. Now the Central Government believes that the provisional congress had no such provisions and has never been held. At the same time, preparations were not completed, so it was decided to change it to the Fifth National Congress on November 12, a formal meeting to discuss and resolve all major issues.

(Dealing with Traitors) When the situation in Tianjin and Beiping was critical, many traitors in Tianjin and Beiping were bought by the Japanese side. The most prominent were Zhang Jingyao, Qi Xieyuan, Sun Chuanfang, and Shi Yousan. Zhang received 1.8 million yuan in Tianjin, specifically to instigate traitors and buy off our army and politicians. After Zhang Jingyao was assassinated, the evidence obtained was colorful and all-encompassing, such as attempting to establish a North China military government, plotting a second puppet state, and so on. These actions not only sacrificed Tianjin and Beiping but also affected the entire country. Therefore, considering the overall situation, a temporary ceasefire was definitely necessary in order to reorganize everything.

Sichuan Fellow-Provincials Association Seeks to Stop the Sichuan War 88

Yesterday's General Meeting of Members

The Anti-War Association Also Sent Members to Attend

The Sichuan Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai was established on May 31st of last year and has now reached its anniversary. Yesterday afternoon, the Second General Meeting of Members was held in the auditorium of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, attended by more than three hundred new and old members, as well as Zhu Yakui, representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, Zeng Zhaomen, representative of the Social Affairs Bureau, Zhu Yunsheng, representative of the Public Security Bureau, Liu Changwei Zhanen, member of the Abolish Civil War Association, and Secretary Gu Shoutang. Chairman Huang Fogong reported the purpose of the meeting.

After the representatives delivered their speeches, Liu Zhanen, representing the Anti-War Association, explained the process of repeatedly stopping the civil war in Sichuan Province. Following that, the association discussed and proposed many motions, and the meeting adjourned at 7:00 PM.

Chairman's Report After the opening of the meeting, Huang Fogong, chairman of the general meeting, first reported the purpose of the meeting, followed by an opening speech, which stated briefly: "Today, our association is holding its second general meeting of members, and we are greatly honored to have the party and government agencies and all sectors come to guide us. From now on, our association should unite with collective wisdom and efforts and repay the country and society."

Representatives' Speeches Then Zhu Yakui, representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, gave a speech, stating briefly: "Your association has only been established for a year, and its achievements are remarkable, which is extremely admirable. From now on, we hope that you will work even harder." Next, Liu Zhanen, representative of the Anti-War Association, gave a speech, stating briefly: "Today, the fellow-provincials of Sichuan in Shanghai are here, joyfully holding a general meeting of members, while our hometown is suffering from the flames of warlord warfare, which is heartbreaking. The Anti-War Association, based on its mission, has repeatedly researched and discussed, and repeatedly telegraphed to appeal for ways to eliminate it, but it has not achieved the greatest effect, which is deeply regrettable. Today, the motions proposed by your association are paying great attention to the Sichuan War, which I am even more deeply moved by. However, abolishing civil war cannot be done by one organization or one local people, but must be done by all the people of the country, uniting together and working together. I deeply hope that your association will cooperate with the Anti-War Association in the future to jointly discuss ways to stop the civil war. Recently, our association requested the central government to stop the transportation of military supplies to Sichuan by any province in order to fundamentally solve the civil war. However, your association must proceed together, such as investigating the origin of the internal strife of the Sichuan warlords and persuading the warlords to discover their conscience. If these points cannot be realized, we should make a firm decision not to cooperate with the Sichuan warlords. First, friendship does not cooperate; if representatives such as Liu Xiang and Liu Wenhui come to Shanghai, we must not pay attention to them. Second, economic cooperation does not cooperate; if they privately import military supplies, you can explore and announce their secrets. Third, make a great determination to go to Sichuan to work hard for national salvation, etc., all of which have a great effect on stopping the civil war."

Discussion of the Sichuan War The meeting believes that the people of Sichuan Province have repeatedly suffered tragic wars due to the internal strife of the warlords, with the people living in misery. Therefore, it proposed to discuss the opposition to the Sichuan warlords continuing the civil war. The resolutions are as follows: (1) Opposition to the Sichuan warlords continuing to fight each other: (A) Telegraph to the central government, ordering the Sichuan warlords to stop fighting immediately and severely punish those who violate the order; (B) Submit a request to the central government to send personnel back to Sichuan to supervise the military to implement the disbandment of the troops; (C) Submit a request to the central government to strictly order two-thirds of the troops under Sichuan's jurisdiction to go to Xikang to consolidate national defense, and one-third to go out of Sichuan to assist in resisting Japan; (D) This association will send a telegram to the people of the whole country to oppose civil war; (E) Send a telegram to all fellow-provincials in Sichuan, to awaken and go on strike to oppose civil war; (F) Request the central government to expel the representatives of the Sichuan warlords stationed in Beijing in the near future; (G) Ask the central government to strictly stop the transportation of military supplies to Sichuan to supply the warlords' civil war; (H) Organize an appraisal committee to confiscate the deposits of the Sichuan warlords stored in Shanghai and various banks in other provinces; (2) Opposition to the Sichuan warlords' imposition of all kinds of exorbitant taxes: (A) This association will submit a request to the central government to order the Sichuan warlords to immediately abolish all kinds of exorbitant taxes; (B)

Send a telegram to all sectors of the people in Sichuan to awaken and go on strike to oppose all kinds of exorbitant taxes; (C) In the future, if any events of opposition to exorbitant taxes occur in Sichuan, this association should provide substantial assistance and send a telegram to the whole country for assistance; (3) Submit a request to the government to issue a notice to schools across the country to exempt students from the "red" areas such as Tong, Nan, and Ba from tuition fees: (A) Submit a request to the government to forward to the Ministry of Education to issue a notice to schools across the country to exempt students from the "red" areas such as Tong, Nan, and Ba from tuition fees; (B) This association will raise donations from fellow-provincials and other people with lofty ideals to help overseas students from Tong, Nan, and Ba and other places who are on the verge of desperation; (C) Request the government to issue a notice to schools to offer full or partial exemption from tuition fees for students in areas affected by natural disasters and war.

Re-electing Officials After the discussion, the officials were re-elected. It was planned to elect 25 executive committee members, 9 alternate members, 15 supervisory committee members, and 7 alternate members. The list was not announced due to the lateness of the hour.

Duan Honggang Describes Duan Qirui's Condition 89

Mr. Duan Is Old and Lacks Energy

The German Doctor Plans to Give a Blood Transfusion

Duan Hongye Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday

The National News Agency reports that Duan Qirui is ill in Shanghai and is being treated by German doctor Mi Aili. The reporter visited Duan's nephew, Mr. Honggang, yesterday and was granted an interview. When asked about Duan's condition, he said that Mr. Duan's illness is not as serious as rumors suggest. Only on the 27th of last month (i.e., the 4th of this month in the lunar calendar), he accidentally coughed up a few mouthfuls of blood, and there was a slight amount of blood in his stool. At that time, Dr. Mi (Aili) was consulted, and it was found that there were slight cracks in the blood vessels in his stomach, which caused the blood to come out of his mouth. That is also where the origin of his coughing up blood lies. However, it stopped after taking medicine. It has been more than ten days since then, and his eating and sleeping have returned to normal. However, he is old and lacks energy, and his blood and nutrition are insufficient after coughing up blood. This is a common phenomenon for patients and is not important. Today (i.e., yesterday), it is planned to wait for the doctor to come again for a diagnosis, and I (Honggang) will give a blood transfusion once, needing an amount of about 300 to 400 cc. The blood in my body has also been diagnosed by the doctor and determined to be usable. Therefore, after Mr. Duan receives the blood transfusion, his physical strength may be even stronger. My older brother, Hongye, arrived in Shanghai from Tianjin at 4:00 PM yesterday. However, he wanted to come south earlier and did not come to Shanghai because of Duan's illness. As for the report in today's newspaper that Mr. Duan is critically ill in Shanghai and that his coffin made of Phoebe nanmu has been transported south from Tianjin, I can truthfully declare that this has not happened. After the conversation, he took his leave and departed.

The Auditing Committee of the Central Mint Will Regularly Inspect New Coins 90

The Second Review Meeting Will Be Held on the 9th

The Auditing Committee for New Coins of the Central Mint was announced last month and held its first meeting. It is now learned that the committee is scheduled to hold its second auditing meeting at 4:30 PM on the 9th of this month on the third floor of the Central Bank. At that time, the following motions will be discussed: (1) Draft rules of procedure; (2) Appoint a chemical analyst to chemically analyze the fineness of the new coins; (3) Assess the factory's affairs and audit the accounts. It is heard that the inspection method will be to randomly select one or two coins from every 10,000 new coins cast for chemical analysis. If their fineness and weight comply with the law, a certificate will be issued and they will be allowed to circulate on the market; otherwise, they will be remelted and recast. Currently, the factory's new coin molds can produce more than 200,000 yuan per day. Once the inspection is qualified, they can be circulated on the market.

Representatives Petitioning for the Refund of Artificial Silk Import Tax Will Enter Beijing Tonight 91

Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Chinese Industrial General Federation

Helping the Silk Industry Send Members to Beijing to Petition Together

The Shanghai Motor Silk Weaving Factory and the Silk and Satin Industry Association, in view of the severe decline in the foreign trade of silk fabrics, plan to ask the government to refund the import tax on artificial silk in order to reduce costs and help the industry. On the 21st of last month, the two industries held a joint meeting and decided to organize a petition delegation, scheduled to enter Beijing by train on the night of June 5th, stay at the Central Hotel, and go to various ministries and courtyards the next day to petition. At the same time, they sent letters to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Chinese Industrial Federation, requesting them to send additional representatives to provide assistance. At its 37th standing committee meeting, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce decided to publicly recommend Wang Yansong, a standing committee member, as a supporting representative to accompany them to Beijing. The Chinese Industrial Federation, especially because the refund of the artificial silk import tax concerns the life and death of the entire Chinese silk industry, expressed great sympathy for participating in the petition. They also notified the Suzhou-Hangzhou branch earlier, invited silk merchants to come to Shanghai, and convened a discussion meeting at the general association at No. 9 Hankou Road at 4:00 PM yesterday, and recommended Qian Chengxu to be a representative to go to Beijing to depart together. It can be seen that this request to the government to refund the artificial silk import tax is to save the industry from bankruptcy, and the survival of the silk weaving and silk satin industries in our country is deeply and greatly related. Therefore, all industrial and commercial organizations in this city attach great importance to the progress of this case and do not hesitate to sacrifice their spirit and express their strength to assist. The prospect of the petition is very promising. It is thought that there will be an even more enthusiastic atmosphere when the petition delegation departs from Shanghai.

The Case of Inspecting Factories in the Concession Will Continue to Be Discussed This Week 92

Hoping for a Smooth Resolution

Regarding the negotiation of the right to inspect factories in the Public Concession, Yu Hongjun, Secretary-General of the Municipal Government, and Fessenden, Director-General of the Municipal Council, once exchanged views unofficially last month, and after preliminary consultations, their views were quite close. Dumping of Russian Goods in China 93

Major Commercial Ports Will Add Commercial Agencies

The Central News Agency reports that since the restoration of diplomatic relations between China and Russia, the Russian Merchants Assistance Association in this city has been actively seeking ways to dump Russian goods in China. Therefore, Lai Wen, manager of the association, returned to the Russian capital last month to discuss the transportation of Russian goods to China with the Russian government's commercial authorities. It is also heard that the Russian Merchants Assistance Association will add commercial agencies in major commercial ports in our country after Lai Wen returns to Shanghai.

Alliance of Six Shipping Companies

Major Changes in River Shipping in Sichuan, Chinese Small Steamers Are All Defeated 94

Since the alliance of the six major companies in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, the small steamer companies operating between Yichang and Chongqing have all been defeated. Of the ten or so shipping companies, only one or two are currently operating. Director Ren of the Yichang Shipping Association came to Shanghai from the Sichuan River and informed us of the current situation of shipping in the Yichang-Chongqing area, which is described as follows: Cooperation of Six Companies River shipping from Shanghai to Yichang and from Yichang to Chongqing. Shanghai has no direct ships to Chongqing. Therefore, there were many Chinese ships operating on the Yichang-Chongqing route. At its peak, there were seventeen or eighteen companies. Since last year, foreign merchant ships in Shanghai, such as Jardine Matheson, Taikoo, etc., have added direct routes to Chongqing in the upper reaches, monopolizing the goods transported from Shanghai to the Sichuan River, making it impossible for the small steamer companies on the Yichang-Chongqing route to support themselves. They have stopped sailing one after another, and Minsheng Company has raised funds to buy the Chinese ships that have stopped sailing to form a new force of Chinese merchants in the Sichuan River. From then on, the Yichang-Chongqing route has been transformed into the Shanghai-Chongqing route. Taikoo, Jardine Matheson, China Merchants Sanbei, and Minsheng are the six companies that have implemented cooperative operations.

Increasing the Price of Shanghai-Yichang Shipping All six companies' river ships in Sichuan have been changed to direct Shanghai-Chongqing routes. The Yichang-Chongqing section is now only operated by Jufu, Yihua, Yongfu, and other companies. In order to compete for the Sichuan River shipping industry and maintain the long-term interests of the Shanghai-Chongqing route, the six companies have repeatedly reduced the water freight rate on the Shanghai-Chongqing route, from twelve taels to seven taels. At the same time, the rate from Yichang to Chongqing has been increased to six taels, so that Shanghai customers will transport goods to Sichuan directly from Shanghai.

Sale of Small Steamers Due to the alliance of the six companies, direct Shanghai-Chongqing routes have been created, causing the old route from Yichang to Chongqing to become naturally abandoned and eliminated. Now the Yongyou steamship, which operates on the Yichang-Chongqing route, has no wharf warehouse in Shanghai and is heard to be sold to a Chinese steamship company in Shanghai, while the Yongnian and Yongfeng ships will be bought by Minsheng Company. From then on, no Chinese ships will operate on the Yichang-Chongqing route. The Sichuan River shipping industry will soon be operated by the six companies.

Sharp Decline in Business Due to the situation in Sichuan, many merchants are hesitant to handle goods, and the exchange rate between Sichuan and Shanghai currencies is that every 1,000 yuan of Shanghai currency requires more than 1,600 yuan of Sichuan currency. Due to the unfavorable exchange rate, they have stopped handling goods, and business has declined to an extreme degree. In addition, Liu Xiang's ban prohibits the export of cash, and anyone who privately exports 10 yuan of silver will be severely punished if caught. Therefore, business is even more affected. Taikoo and Jardine Matheson have each reduced one ship, and the Sanbei Wuxing ship is currently under repair and will be opened soon. However, it is heard that Japanese ships in Sichuan that have been stopped for a year and a half are now planning to resume sailing.

Qianye Business Research Association Established

Qin Runqing and Fifteen Others Elected as Directors 96

Shanghai Qianye (banking industry) colleagues Qin Runqing, Fu Songnian, Yu Zuoting, Wang [omitted], [omitted], etc., in response to the needs of the times, initiated the organization of a business research association. After submitting it to and passing it through the Qianye members' congress, more than 240 employees of the same industry who were supposed to join had a meeting the other day, established the association, and elected fifteen directors. Yesterday, a meeting was held at the guild hall, and Qin Runqing, Qin [omitted], Yu Zuoting, Pei Yunqing, Wang [omitted], Lu Shuchen, Wang Geng, Fu Songnian, Yan Dayou, Du Pingfu, Xu Boxiong, He Zhongxiao, Feng Yigui, Lin Rongsheng, Xi Jiming, and others were elected with a majority vote, while Hu Zuan, Lin Ruiting, and six others were elected as alternates. The full text of the eight articles of the constitution is as follows: Article 1: Name. This association is named the Shanghai Qianye Business Research Association, with its address inside the Shanghai Qianye Guild Hall. Article 2: Purpose. The purpose of this association is to research Qianye academics and promote Qianye business. Article 3: Affairs. This association will research the following affairs: (1) Matters concerning the promotion and innovation of the Qianye industry; (2) Matters concerning lectures and education in the Qianye industry; (3) Other matters concerning the Qianye industry. Article 4: Members. All members of the Shanghai Qianye Guild Hall and employees of the Yuan Zi Zhuang can become members of this association. Employees of other Qian Zhuang who wish to apply for membership must be introduced by two or more members of this association and approved by the board of directors to become members of this association. Article 5: Leaving the Association. If a member of this association has any of the following circumstances, they may be declared to have left the association after a resolution by the members' congress: (1) Engaging in improper conduct that harms the reputation of this association; (2) Changing jobs; (3) Voluntarily requesting to leave the association. Article 6: Staff. This association shall have fifteen directors, who shall be elected from among the members. The directors shall then elect a director-general from among themselves. The term of office for directors is one year, and they may be re-elected. Article 7: Meetings. The meetings of this association are divided into the following two types: (1) Members' Congress: (A) Regular meeting, held once a month, and scheduled to be held at 7:00 PM on the 16th of each month; (B) Special meeting, convened at any time when the board of directors deems it necessary, or at the request of one-tenth or more of the members; (2) Regular Board Meeting, convened as determined by the board of directors. Article 8: Supplementary Provisions. Matters not covered in this charter may be amended by a resolution of the Members' Congress.

Red Swastika Society Relieves Tangshan Refugees 101

The Shanghai General Office of the Red Swastika Society received a telegram from Beijing yesterday. The Beijing General Association of the Society received a letter from the Tangshan Tenth Relief Team stationed in Tangshan, stating briefly that during the recent turmoil in Tangshan, bandits took the opportunity to loot, and the people's homes were completely emptied. The people fled in a panic. The cruelty and suffering were unprecedented. The team members went out to provide relief and took in more than 1,900 refugee women and children. A total of more than 3,700 women and children were sheltered in the four locations. Because the relief personnel were insufficient, additional personnel were sent to the treatment centers and shelters to treat more than 500 wounded and sick soldiers and civilians in rotation. Now the situation in the area has stabilized slightly, and more than 900 refugees, women, and children have returned home. However, 2,800 refugees still remain in the four locations. After returning home, they found their homes completely emptied. They lack clothing and food. Those whose houses were destroyed by artillery fire live in makeshift shelters, exposed to the wind and rain. The need for relief is extremely urgent.

Red Swastika Society Sends Personnel to Northern Anhui for Epidemic Prevention 102

Organizing Burial Teams | | | Going to Huoshan to Work

The Red Swastika Society has repeatedly received letters and telegrams from the head of Zhufuoan in Huoshan, reporting that there are more than 18,000 corpses of people who died tragically in the river beach of Zhufuoan Mountain in Huoshan. When they were killed, most of them were decapitated, or dismembered. The various tragic scenes were unbearable to witness. Afterwards, local people buried them in sand and soil in 130 large piles. However, the river beach is not a suitable place to bury bones. Once mountain floods occur, the corpses will be washed away and will inevitably float along the Huai River to the Yangtze River, which will inevitably cause a major epidemic. The Shanghai General Office of the Society, in view of this, specially sent Commissioner Zhao Yulin to Hefei and Liu'an to negotiate the organization of a large-scale burial team to relocate these more than 10,000 remains within the shortest possible time to prevent future epidemics. It is heard that Commissioner Zhao arrived in Hefei a few days ago and began to organize the team, and will depart for Huoshan to work immediately.

The Court's Instructions in the Gao Yatou Case: It is Inappropriate to Summon Witnesses Again According to the Agreement 104

| Barbers' Association to Hold Emergency Meeting Today |

In the case of the French Concession Western police officer Miller kicking Gao Yatou to death, after negotiations between the Yangzhou Fellow Villagers Association and the Barbers' Association, it is now learned that the Jiangsu Shanghai Second Special District Local Court yesterday issued instructions to Gao's father, Gao Yuanlin, stating, "Da Zi No. 51, original plaintiff Gao Yuanlin, one document presented. Gao Yuanlin's request to summon witnesses in the case of Gao Yatou's death is noted. After reviewing the investigation procedures of this court, it has long been completed. As the case does not fall within the scope of Articles 103 to 186 of the Criminal Code, according to the agreement on the establishment of a Chinese court in the French Concession, this court is indeed unable to summon witnesses again. If the civilian believes that it is necessary to summon witnesses, they should directly apply to the Concession authorities according to the agreement. This instruction, June 2nd of the 22nd year of the Republic of China, Chief Prosecutor Chen Beisan." In addition to the Yangzhou Fellow Villagers Association scheduling another meeting to discuss how to negotiate in the future since the court cannot summon witnesses again, the Barbers' Association decided to hold a plenary committee meeting at the Xieqiao South First Public Office at 10:00 AM today to discuss the final response measures and report on the progress of petitions to various agencies.

Shanghai Finance Bureau Issues Notice to Strictly Prevent Counterfeit House Tax Receipts 109

Cai Zengji, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau, recently found that criminals were forging house tax receipts to defraud citizens of donations. In addition to requesting the Public Security Bureau to send detectives to investigate strictly, he issued Notice No. 216 yesterday, stating, "Regarding the matter of notice, it has recently been reported by the Municipal South District Tax Collection Office of this Bureau that it has been discovered that there are forged house tax receipts of this Bureau to defraud donations, and requested a review and handling, and to find ways to prevent it. After investigating, the house tax receipts of this Bureau have always had a fixed format and change the color of the paper every quarter to distinguish them. There are precautions printed on the back of the receipts, and the address and amount of the donation are filled in on the front, and stamped with the seal of this Bureau to show solemnity. When citizens pay the house tax, they should verify whether the seal on the donation ticket is the same as the one stamped in the previous quarter, and they may ask the collector to see the employee certificate issued by this Bureau with their photo affixed to it. If there is any doubt or definite counterfeit house tax receipts, they should immediately hand them over to the police on duty for handling. In addition to separately ordering strict investigation and reporting to the Municipal Government for review, this notice is urgently issued, and all citizens should be informed. Be sure to comply."

A Woman Commits Suicide by Hanging Due to Debt Disputes 112

The Police Request an Autopsy

The Family Tries to Avoid It

Zhang Shen, a woman from Funing living at No. 9 Hengchang Lane, Binlang Road, was only 23 years old. Because she had borrowed money from Xu Jiang, a fellow villager at No. 7 next door, and was unable to repay it, Xu Jiang went to demand the debt again on the first of this month, resulting in a conflict with Zhang Shen. After being persuaded to disperse, Zhang Shen's anger did not subside, so she bought opium and swallowed it at 3:00 PM that afternoon. When her family noticed, they quickly sent her to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment, but the poison had already attacked her heart and could not be saved. She died that day, and her family prepared a coffin to collect her body. The Puto Road police learned of this and believed that the case involved human life and should be thoroughly investigated. They immediately carried the coffin to the autopsy station on Peel Road. Yesterday morning, they reported to Guo Wei, the prosecutor of the First Special District Local Court, to come to the station. The police also requested lawyer Qian Xunjiu to represent them in requesting an autopsy. However, Zhang Shen's aunt, Zhang Shen, and her uncle, Shen Qidong, both requested to be exempt from the autopsy, saying that the deceased had taken poison on her own and there was no other reason. They represented the maternal family and the husband's family, respectively, and had no objections. However, the police believed that in order to clarify the cause of death, an autopsy was necessary, so they requested Prosecutor Guo to approve it so that they could proceed immediately. Mr. Guo believed that the matter was of great importance and needed to be carefully considered before a decision could be made, so he did not immediately perform the autopsy.

Li Afu is the Worst of Ruffians 114

Harassing a Weak Woman and Daring to Commit Assault

Sentenced to Six Months in Prison

Chen Yueying, a woman from Wenzhou, is twenty-eight years old and has a beautiful appearance. Her family lives in the Aizhulin tourist area at No. 23, Lane 446, Huade Road. At 10:30 PM the night before, she was at home playing cards with her brother, Chen Laosan, and others when Li Afu, a fellow villager, came to chat. Seeing Yueying's delicate and exquisite appearance, he flirted with her in every possible way. When the card game ended, Li Afu forcibly pulled the woman's hand, asking her to go somewhere to play, and provoking her with obscene words. The woman angrily told her brother about the situation. Chen Laosan was furious and asked him sternly. Afu refused to show weakness and spoke disrespectfully. Chen Laosan slapped him once. Afu was ashamed and unable to bear it. He took out a small foreign knife from his pocket and stabbed Laosan three times in the left chest, and fled out the door. The woman was shocked and ran to tell her elder brother Laoer, who chased and caught Afu and fought each other. The Chinese police officer No. 1444 of the lane heard the alarm and arrived, and after learning the details, helped to arrest Li Afu and sent him to the Yulin Road police station. The head of the police station ordered him to be detained. The police also ordered the detectives to send the injured to Tongren Hospital for treatment by car. The next morning, the police sent the suspect Li to the third criminal court of the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin described the course of events in detail, and said that the suspect's knife was discarded by him at the time and could not be found. He asked for an investigation, and presented the victim's bloody clothes for inspection. Chen Laosan's injuries were still light, and after being bandaged by the doctor, he went to court to complain about the suspect's assault. His elder brother Chen Laoer and his younger sister Chen Yueying testified to the facts. When questioned, the defendant's confession was evasive, and he denied stabbing Chen Laosan with a knife, saying that there were many people who beat him at that time, and he asked for leniency. Judge Wu Zehan, because the evidence was conclusive, and there was no room for sophistry, sentenced Li Afu to six months' imprisonment as a warning.

Dismissed Constable Impersonating Official to Extort Money 116

Wei Dingshan, a native of Jiangbei, thirty years old this year, formerly served as Hua constable No. 244 in the French Concession police force. Because during an assignment, he privately embezzled a certain Mr. Jia's opium and forcibly stripped Mr. Jia of his clothes, the police force investigated and immediately dismissed him. Afterwards, Wei became unemployed. Unexpectedly, recently, Wei had another bizarre idea. In the area of McDonald Road and Jules Pasteurs Road in the New Concession, whenever he saw someone defecating in the wasteland, he would impersonate a plainclothes detective from the police force and extort money. Countless people have been fooled. On the morning of the day before yesterday, at 5:30 AM, Qiu Miaogen, who lived at Liu's residence on McDonald Road, and Wang Awu, who lived at No. 7 Wule Lane on McDonald Road, were defecating in a nearby open space when Wei saw them. Wei approached them and said, "How dare you defecate here? I am a plainclothes detective from the police force." After saying this, he detained the two of them, as if intending to take them to the police station. First, Qiu Miaogen pleaded with him, offering to pay a bribe of six jiao in foreign currency to be released. Wei feigned disapproval. Qiu increased the offer to one yuan, and Wei finally agreed to release him. Wang, however, had no money to bribe, which led to a dispute. Coincidentally, Chinese constables Nos. 381, 104, and 196 from the Avenue Edward VII police station were patrolling and saw what was happening. They approached and inquired. Wei changed his story and impersonated a sanitation worker, speaking evasively. Therefore, the constables detained Wei and took him to the police station. He was then sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court. First, the police lawyer, Yao Zhaodi, explained the case, stating that the police force was prosecuting the defendant under Article 370 of the Criminal Code. Then, the plaintiffs, Qiu Miaogen and Wang Awu, recounted the previous events. When questioned, Wei Dingshan admitted to impersonating a public official and extorting money. After Judge Zhang reviewed the confession, he ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody and rescheduled the sentencing.

Indian Criminal Opens Fire, Refusing Arrest 119

Stray Bullet Wounds Russian Constable and Rickshaw Puller

Yesterday at 10:45 PM, the Public Concession Police Department dispatched Chinese and Western detectives, traveling in a car, to report to the special agency of the French Concession Police on Rue Massenet, stating that three Indian criminal suspects had been spotted watching a movie at the Golden Grand Theater at the corner of Rue du Consulat and Rue de Saigon, and requested assistance in their apprehension. Upon receiving the report, the police chief immediately dispatched Russian Constable No. 44, along with several Chinese and Annamite detectives, to the address. Upon arriving at the destination, the detectives waited outside the theater. At 11:15 PM, as the theater emptied and people streamed out, the three Indian suspects emerged from the crowd. The detectives immediately moved in to arrest them, capturing two of the suspects on the spot. The other suspect resisted fiercely. As an Annamite detective grabbed him, the suspect struggled to escape, fleeing south. He pulled a handgun from his pocket and resisted arrest. The detectives also drew their guns and returned fire. Both sides exchanged six or seven shots. A bullet grazed the forehead of Russian Constable No. 44, and a stray bullet wounded a rickshaw puller in the leg. As a result, the suspect ultimately escaped. The detectives then took the two Indian suspects to the Rue Massenet police station. After a brief interrogation by the police chief, he ordered them to be handed over to the detectives who had reported the information. The wounded Russian constable and rickshaw puller were taken to the hospital for treatment.

Sworn Brothers Commit Suicide by Poisoning 120

Wang Wenxiu, 25 years old, from Wuxi, and his fellow townsman Wu Dongfen, 23 years old, were sworn brothers. Both were unemployed and in dire straits. They conceived the idea of suicide. Last night, they checked into Room 5 of the Tianyuan Hotel at No. 78 Xiamen Road and both ingested opium to end their lives. Later, the hotel staff discovered them and reported to the police station. An ambulance was dispatched and they were sent to Renji Hospital for treatment. Fortunately, the rescue was timely, and they are now out of danger.

Tea Party at the China International Library 121

The Geneva China International Library held a tea party yesterday (4th) at 5:00 PM, after the close of the World Culture Cooperation China Association, at the reading room of its Shanghai office, for invited guests. Among the participants were Kong Yongzhi, Zhu Jiasen, Li Runzhang, Cai Yuanpei, Wu Zhihui, Wang Yiting, Zhou Zuomin, as well as prominent figures from the financial, educational, and artistic circles. Mr. Cai Yuanpei presided and delivered a speech, stating that Chinese culture has a history of thousands of years, and the invention of printing was earlier than in other countries. However, because our country lacks the materials to present to the world, other countries have not been able to have a deep understanding of us. Now, the China International Library is engaged in this work, so that Chinese and Western cultures can be connected, and the future of world cooperation will depend on this. Next, Mr. Cui Zhuhan read Mr. Zhang Jingjiang's congratulatory message. Then, Mr. Wu Zhihui delivered a speech, saying that although the world today has no justice, we must firmly believe in the existence of justice. If we want to see justice prevail, then we must first gain the sympathy of those who have it in the international community. Therefore, various international cooperation projects are of great benefit to us. The China International Library contributes systematic materials to the international community, so that people can have a deeper understanding of us. This is fortunate for world cooperation and for justice. Finally, Mr. Li Shizeng, in his capacity as a representative, reported on the establishment of the China International Library in great detail. Mr. Li first described the motivation for establishing the China International Library, then described the role of its establishment, and finally stated his hopes for the library, and hoped that all sectors would provide guidance and help. After the report was completed, the guests spoke, with Mr. Xu Jingren and others giving concise speeches, and immediately agreeing to serve as founders of the library, so that everyone can work together to achieve complete success. Then, Mr. Li Shizeng led a tour of the rooms. The guests praised the exquisite arrangement and comprehensive equipment of the various departments, and it was 8 o'clock when the meeting ended.

Ji Zhang Commits Suicide 125

| Wang Desheng's Actual |

Ji Zhang, a 43-year-old woman from Yancheng, was married to Ji Siya, who farmed in their hometown. They had two sons. The elder son, Ji Buquan, 20 years old, was married to Chen, 18 years old. The younger son was named Xiaohongzi, 13 years old. Unexpectedly, Ji Siya fell ill and died at home on August 5th last year, losing the family's support. Ji Buquan was introduced by a friend to work in Longyan County. Ji Zhang, along with her younger son Xiaohongzi and daughter-in-law Ji Chen, came to Shanghai to make a living in January of this year. They built a thatched shed along the Hongqiao in the western part of Shanghai to live in. Her son and daughter-in-law went to work in nearby rope factories. Ji Zhang cooked and washed for her son and daughter-in-law at home, and although they were poor, they felt amiable. In a thatched shed at No. 38 nearby, there was a Shandong man, Wang Desheng, 42 years old, who had no profession and was a rogue. His wife died of illness in January, so he was bored all day and chatted with Ji Zhang's family. Because one was a widower and the other was a new widow, an ambiguity soon arose. In February, the two families merged into one. However, Wang Desheng was brutal and often beat them. At 10 PM the day before yesterday, Ji Zhang and her daughter-in-law went to bed separately. Unexpectedly, Wang Desheng, with a human face but a beast's heart, had long coveted his daughter-in-law, Chen. He sneaked to Chen's bed and raped her. Chen woke up and screamed. Ji Zhang heard the sound and rushed over. Seeing this situation, she was very angry. She pulled Wang Desheng off her and scolded him. Wang became angry and, out of shame, used a sandalwood stick that he usually played with to beat Ji Zhang severely, causing her to be bruised all over and her face covered in blood. Neighbors came out to persuade them, but Wang was unreasonable and poured urine and feces from the chamber pot, so no one could persuade him. At 10:00 AM the next day, Ji Zhang suddenly died. Everyone was shocked and rushed to see her. Ji Zhang committed suicide by hanging herself. Wang untied the body. A rope was taken away by a lottery gambler to pray for a dream. When Ji Chen and Ji Xiaohongzi returned home and saw their mother's tragic death, they went to the Second District Police Station to accuse Wang of murder. The police were dispatched to arrest Wang. According to Wang, the deceased committed suicide because she was angry and tired of the world, and he did not murder or coerce her. The district sent Gu Xueyuan, a local security officer from the Fifth District, to report to the local court. Prosecutor Ouyang came to inspect and determined that she had committed suicide by hanging herself after being injured, and ordered the body to be collected and an investigation to be conducted.

Initiating the Establishment of a Leprosy Hospital 129

Charitable and Medical Circles Raise Funds

The Ministry of Health Will Also Organize a Leprosy Association

The facilities for leprosy hospitals are very lacking in various parts of our country, and according to surveys by the medical community, there are nearly one million people in the country suffering from this disease. Therefore, the medical and charitable communities of this port, in view of the terrible contagiousness of leprosy, have decided to raise huge sums of money from all sectors to establish a fully equipped leprosy hospital for the benefit of society. The details are as follows:

Infectious areas According to surveys by the medical community, there are a total of two million leprosy patients worldwide, and leprosy patients in our country account for half of them. According to reliable data, among the people of various provinces suffering from this disease, Fujian and Guangdong have the most, followed by Guizhou, followed by Anhui, Hubei, Hunan, Jiangxi, and other provinces. Shandong, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang rank fifth, and Gansu ranks sixth. The three northeastern provinces have the fewest. People in other provinces rarely suffer from this disease.

Local facilities As for the establishment of leprosy hospitals in our country, according to a survey of the whole country, Jiangxi has Nanchang Leprosy Hospital, Fujian has Yanping Leprosy Hospital, Guangdong has Beihai Leprosy Hospital, and Qiongya Leprosy Hospital on Hainan Island. There are only more than ten hospitals in total, which can accommodate more than 2,000 people. Xiamen and other places are in the process of preparation. There is also no hospital in this port that specializes in this disease. Only the Hongkou Skin Hospital also treats this disease.

Recent Developments The fundraising for the establishment of leprosy hospitals in our country began in 1925, when the American Leprosy Relief Association sent General Manager Tanner to China to carry out publicity. It is now known that the charitable and medical communities of this port have decided to initiate fundraising from all sectors to establish a fully equipped leprosy hospital in Shanghai. It is also heard that the Ministry of Health of the National Government will organize a Central Leprosy Association in the near future.

Russian Who Shot and Killed Indian Doctor Found Not Guilty Due to Mental Illness 130

But Sent to Prison for Confinement Due to Mental Illness

Police Lawyer Requests Reservation of Right to Appeal

Youergaosha Tuoteni Gaofu, a 24-year-old Russian residing at No. 33, Alley 222, Avenue Albert, French Concession, entered the home of British Indian doctor Tai Xiejiara (transliteration) at No. 120 Rue Luban, French Concession, with a handgun at around 3:00 PM on January 4th of this year and shot Tai Xiejiara to death. Later, his brother Yulaijie (transliteration) reported to the French Concession Police, who dispatched detectives to arrest Youergaosha and send him to the Second Special District Local Court. The police lawyer filed a public prosecution based on the crime of homicide under the Criminal Code. Judge Xiong Huicheng repeatedly opened the court to interrogate the defendant, who admitted that he went to the deceased for treatment for a stomach illness. After taking the medicine, he developed erectile dysfunction and killed him out of hatred. Subsequently, the defendant's defense lawyers, Xu Yannian, etc., argued that the defendant suffered from mental illness, causing nervous disorder, and therefore the crime was excusable. They requested the appointment of a well-known doctor to identify the defendant's condition, etc. The court ordered the appointment of a doctor for identification. After examining the circumstances of his confession, it was recorded in the previous report that the court had appointed a specialist in mental illness, a Western doctor named Dalai (transliteration), who was designated by the First Special District Court to specialize in the identification of neurological diseases. After a long period of examination, and with the joint appraisal of the Municipal Council's doctors, the defendant was confirmed to have mental illness, and at the time of the incident, he was in a state of extreme nervous disorder. After the doctor issued an appraisal report to the court, a hearing was held again a few days ago, and the debate was declared over. The police lawyer, Yuan Jiahan, appeared in court at 3:00 PM the day before yesterday for sentencing. The judge presided over the first criminal court and ordered the defendant to be brought to the court. The defendant, Youergaosha Tuoteni Gaofu, was found not guilty because he suffered from mental illness and was ordered to be detained in prison and sent to an asylum. At that time, the police lawyer immediately requested the reservation of the right to appeal in court, which was approved by the court. After the sentencing, the defendant was escorted to the Second Special District Prison by the bailiffs.

Tianjin to Establish Italian Merchant Sports Ground 131

Mr. Airlie Joe of Lihua Foreign Company, Mr. Joe Laiqi, director of the Shanghai Central Sports Ground, and Mr. Shen Changgeng, chairman of the Shanghai Chinese Securities Exchange, will establish an Italian merchant sports ground in the Italian Concession of Tianjin in accordance with Italian law. The articles of association have been formulated and submitted to the Italian Consulate in Shanghai for record. The ground occupies about six acres and a building will be constructed for ball games and other sports, such as boxing, throwing, skating, tennis, small golf, and various indoor games. There will also be a dining hall, bar, dance hall, rooftop garden, gym, exhibition hall, etc. Permission has been obtained from the Tianjin Italian Concession authorities. The term of establishment is set at ten years. It is heard that the general office will be temporarily set up in Shanghai. Starting from the 6th of this month, the shares will be launched in Shanghai and Tianjin simultaneously. The provisional capital is 1.5 million yuan, divided into 150,000 shares, each share is 10 yuan. The first issue of 70,000 shares, including 15,000 shares, will be used as founding shares for founders and co-organizers and will be distributed separately. This share money will be fully collected as start-up expenses and expenses. The remaining 55,000 shares will be publicly subscribed. Reader's Advisor 141

Why Complain About Heaven and Blame Others? 142

Reply to Mr. Wan from Jinan

Answer: Your letter is written with a tearful tone, viewing the current human society as worthless. Indeed, the current social phenomena easily lead to pessimism, but social happiness is originally obtained through struggle. We have not yet participated in this struggle in the slightest and are already complaining about heaven and blaming others, saying how base and dark society is. Society will naturally bluntly reply: If you don't want it to be base and dark, then hurry up and come in and do something. People who stand by with their hands in their pockets and make sarcastic remarks are not qualified to criticize the current society.

It is true that your family and your mother have been sacrificed in this dark society, but have you ever pursued the reason? You must not have pursued this question, so you can only swallow it whole and scold: "The hearts of the Chinese people are selfish and self-interested to the extreme, without knowing shame, without knowing compassion, especially loving to play tricks, loving to bully the weak, loving to fawn on the strong..." In fact, when a society reaches a turning point, the general phenomena are always like this. However, if you study the history of the French Revolution and the Russian Revolution, you will see that at that time, what one saw and heard was nothing but shamelessness and madness, without a sense of right and wrong. The whole society seemed like a stroke-paralyzed corpse. In fact, this is because the old society has reached its end and is entering the grave, like a symbol of a big storm coming. Suddenly, the sky is dark, and everything stops abruptly, the so-called "ten thousand trees are silent, waiting for the rain to come," is such a phenomenon. The transformation of a new era is very magical. As long as its climax arrives, human self-renewal and morality will immediately increase. However, this kind of sun-like ardent life is definitely not something that people with a retreatist mindset like yours can enjoy, who think of "going to the northwest frontier, close to primitive humans, where one can farm and eat for oneself, forget everything before, and start another life of pleasure." Moreover, this kind of thinking is fundamentally a dream: the current northwest, on one side, is influenced by the socialism of Soviet Russia, and on the other side, is being invaded by the "daily attacks" of a certain imperialism. In the near future, it will either become a continuation of "Outer Mongolia" or a second Northeast, and there is absolutely no place for you, who want to "forget everything before" and "start another life of pleasure," to create a "new Peach Blossom Spring." Moreover, I want to ask you: Do you really believe that Chinese society has only produced one good person like you who is "not base, cunning, and only has an ardent heart"? Frankly speaking, from the way you talk, I know that you are still new to society and cannot withstand the fire of society's great furnace. If you enter society like this, you will soon become like the bad people you are so pained and indignant about. Only those who have stumbled countless times in this evil society, but are still themselves, or even "the nature of ginger and cinnamon, the older the spicier," can stand in the current society, can fight with it, and can transform it. To devote oneself to society and the people, there is nothing that cannot be done anytime, anywhere, in any matter. The ancients also said, "Military affairs, punishment, finance, and grain can all be used to become Yao and Shun." Being a revolutionary leader is certainly a profession; being a small clerk is also a real profession, but it depends on what position you stand on and which direction you are working towards. As for the questions you raised, I will answer them here.

1. The ugliness and baseness of human society are not absolute but relative: they are not immutable but change with the change of social systems. Your understanding of human society is completely emotional and short-sighted. Naturally, it is "one-sided." 2) The happiness and pain of life are also relative and mutually causal. For example, revolution is extremely painful, but seeking liberation and fighting for freedom in a bloodbath is happy. Corrupt officials and greedy bureaucrats, sucking marrow and scraping bones, drinking and eating meat, having proud wives and beautiful concubines, or traitors who sell the country, warlords who harm the people, living in luxury, with gold and jade in front of them, are certainly happy, but one person is fat while the world is thin, one family laughs while the road cries, the people regard them as tyrants, and society hates them like enemies. The heart is uneasy at night, and the fate of being pointed at by thousands of people and dying without disease is inevitable sooner or later. Looking around, it is extremely painful. "To obtain happiness," there is no other way but to worry about what the majority worry about and be happy about what the majority are happy about. This is the standard for struggle. 3) The answer has been seen before, no more repetition.

Speaking of books, you should read the following books thoroughly:
