Store Clerk Communication 204

Several Different Kinds of Questions

Editor Sir:

My circumstances are very poor. I only received two years of junior high school education before dropping out. This spring, I came to Shanghai and became a small shop clerk in a store. Now, I have several matters I would like to ask you about, hoping for your guidance. (A) I feel that my Chinese proficiency is somewhat lacking, making it difficult to deal with social situations effectively. I would like to study Chinese language further. I don't know what books I should buy to read. (B) We should also acquire some basic legal knowledge. I would also like to buy some common legal books to read, but I don't know which ones would be good. (C) Hunan is currently issuing national salvation bonds, with the amount subscribed based on the amount of property owned. My family's property is less than five thousand yuan, but there are one or two local bullies in the town who insist that my family's property is worth more than ten thousand yuan and that we should subscribe to the bond based on that amount. My uncle has requested the county government to conduct a thorough investigation to ensure fairness, but the government and the bullies are in cahoots and refuse to grant my uncle's request. My uncle is at his wit's end, and the matter remains unresolved, causing me great anxiety. I implore you, sir, to help me think of a solution. (D) When my late grandfather was alive, he privately established a charity. It owns over eighty acres of land, and all the income from it has been used for local charitable causes over the years. In addition to paying the regular land tax and local surcharges, should it be responsible for other levies and donations? I respectfully inquire.

Yours sincerely,

Yang Suyun (May 29th)

Editor's Note: The path of Chinese language is profound and mysterious, truly without end. However, apart from those few with literary genius and whose circumstances allow for in-depth study, most people only need to have clear and smooth writing, with words that can convey meaning sufficiently for practical use. Judging from your letter, it is reasonably fluent, but when encountering slightly more complex matters or slightly more convoluted meanings, there is inevitably the difficulty of words not adequately expressing your thoughts. It is, of course, good to be open to learning; however, since you are already employed in society, the time you can devote to self-study each day must be limited, and there is so much that a person should study. Therefore, we advise you not to buy several books specifically for studying Chinese language. Fortunately, Chinese people have many opportunities to come into contact with Chinese language, such as the daily newspapers, various valuable magazines, and books introducing various types of knowledge. They can all express very complex matters and very convoluted meanings using very concise words. You only need to carefully understand them while reading, asking yourself whether you could write the same matter or the same meaning as clearly and distinctly. In this way, you can gain a lot of knowledge, and your Chinese proficiency can also improve imperceptibly.

Basic legal knowledge is indeed something that every citizen of a country governed by law should know. Now, I will introduce a few valuable books that I can think of at the moment. (1) "Legal Knowledge," edited by Guo Wei and published by Huiwentang, is worth buying and reading. The content of this book is not very rich, but it provides a reasonable introduction to each area of the law, and it can also provide insights into legal research. Therefore, for people who have never read a law book, it is most suitable to read it first. (2) "General Principles of Criminal Law" (3) "Specific Principles of Criminal Law." These two books are also published by Huiwentang and edited by lawyer Guo Wei. They provide not only a very detailed analysis of the "Criminal Law of the Republic of China" but also discuss its merits and demerits based on legal theory, making them essential reading. As for civil law, procedural law, and others, they are either too complex or not the basic knowledge necessary for the average citizen. I will not introduce them one by one. Fortunately, the book "Legal Knowledge" provides appropriate book recommendations. If you are interested in in-depth study, you can buy them and study them according to its guidance.

If citizens feel that their country truly has admirable aspects, then when national crises arise, they will naturally donate generously and devote themselves to the cause of national salvation. Sadly, in China over the past few decades, the general population has been made somewhat averse to the country by the perverse actions of the ruling authorities, making it difficult for patriotism to arise. Therefore, the fact that these national salvation bonds are being issued through the method of forced contributions is already extremely pitiful. However, it can still be said that national crises are unavoidable; if those who are implementing the policy still engage in underhanded dealings, acting unfairly and illegally, then the public's view of the nation will become increasingly disappointing day by day. Therefore, this matter not only affects the burden on individual families but also indirectly harms the future of the country. This matter should be resisted to the death. If they use the power of the government to oppress you, then you can only resort to prayer.

As for privately established charitable organizations, they are legally referred to as "corporate foundations" and have the same status as "natural persons." Therefore, they have a general obligation to bear all public duties equally.

Novel

The Life of the Five Beauties (2) (24) (Continued) 205

— Ling He

Twenty-Two. The Two Giants

A familiar car horn sounded outside the door. Wu Gui carefully went to open the door himself. It turned out to be Minister Su and a guest. This guest was Mr. Gu, the manager of the Taiwan Bank, whom Wu Gui also knew very well.

They got out of the car one after the other. The master's satin robe even dragged on the running board. Only Manager Gu was wearing a black suit, so of course, it wouldn't drag on the running board, but the tall black top hat bumped against the car roof.

It was already ten o'clock in the evening, and they were still happily running over, undoubtedly having danced a lot in the ballroom. This was because Manager Gu had always loved socializing with foreigners, so all his actions had become Westernized. As soon as he entered the hall, the master asked repeatedly:

"Where's Madam? Where's Madam? Where did she go?"

"She said that the master wasn't coming again, and she was bored, so she went to see a movie."

Wu Gui stood cautiously to the side, answering. The master smiled and glanced at Manager Gu, snorting through his nose, looking as if he wasn't very happy. Then, Manager Gu said playfully: "I didn't expect Geng Weng to still have peach blossom luck in his old age. Look, as soon as you don't come, that peerless beauty will..."

"...inevitably be bored, truly pitiful."

"Nonsense, nonsense!"

Happy laughter, triumphant laughter, but also a wink at Wu Gui. Wu Gui naturally understood the rules of the officialdom and immediately retreated respectfully. However, he didn't dare run too far away, lest there be a need to serve tea or water and no one would respond. He had no choice but to wait quietly outside the door. However, he could still hear the sound of their conversation from the crack in the door. But they were speaking very quietly, and Manager Gu was speaking Japanese, so Wu Gui was naturally at a loss. However, there were sometimes Chinese words mixed in, such as "treaty" and "plan." Wu Gui naturally assumed that they were confidential national matters, and he didn't need to inquire about them. But his master was speaking Mandarin, but also very quietly, and it was difficult to hear clearly. As far as Wu Gui knew, Minister Su could not only speak Japanese but also French. However, he didn't speak them, probably because he was old and didn't want to bother. Of course, foreign languages were never as convenient as his native language. However, Wu Gui still carefully eavesdropped on a few sentences:

"...this point is exactly the same as what I meant: I believe that if we can merge and establish a country according to this plan, it will indeed surprise the white race. If Asia truly unites... But this matter always feels difficult to implement. At the same time, this amount of activity funding is still not enough..."

Wu Gui didn't understand what it meant. Looking at the pocket watch on his body, it was already eleven forty-five. Madam should be back. So he immediately went to the door and told the gatekeeper:

"You must guard carefully. When Madam comes back, you must tell her that the master is waiting inside, tell her to..."

"...go in through the door in Mr. Zhang's opium den. Did you hear clearly?"

THE AHN N PAO BOROON BOOTLON

The Possibilities for Wealthy Women on the Silver Screen 206

— Xun Nan

To Become a Star, One Must Work Hard and Strive for Self-Improvement

Wealthy Women Lack the Spirit to Strive

Can wealthy women become stars on the silver screen? This is a question that requires much thought. Working under carbon arc lights certainly offers not only substantial monetary income but also fame that overflows the universe. Therefore, many people believe that those who enter the film industry do not necessarily come solely for profit but also for fame. Those without money come for money, but those with money can also come for fame. This sounds very reasonable, but in fact, it is not. Wealthy women, on a whim, run to Hollywood. However, even those who possess not only the power of money and the splendor of clothing but also beautiful faces and graceful figures have failed. What is the reason? Acting is not easy. One must not only work hard and diligently but also endure the temper of directors and colleagues, refining oneself for years before becoming a luminary. Therefore, women without money look at the stars who have already made a name for themselves, earning tens of thousands in salaries, and they are filled with envy and encourage themselves to climb upwards cautiously, gradually rising above others and becoming stars. As for wealthy women, firstly, they are used to comfort and naturally cannot temper their bodies and strive for advancement. Secondly, they do not lack money and naturally do not envy the large salaries of others, lacking a forward-driving force.

As for talented actresses, they are naturally another matter. However, where do so many geniuses come from who do not need to go through training? It's just that some women are smarter and advance faster than others, so everyone calls them "geniuses." Clara Bow, Greta Garbo, and Joan Crawford, weren't they all trained?

Now, there is a new actress in Hollywood named Adrienne Ames. She abandoned her wealthy family and ran to Hollywood, determined to become a star. She carefully analyzed the various reasons for the past failures of wealthy women in Hollywood. She understood the harm of having money and strived for advancement. Now, she is gradually showing her talent and has become a supporting actress for Shepherd. She herself said that she came to Hollywood not because of a whim but because she wanted to be self-reliant and make a difference. She can continue to work without stopping because of small achievements, so her future is very promising. However, when she first arrived in Hollywood, who didn't treat her as a rich dilettante? Who would seriously consider her intentions?

Before entering the film industry, Adrienne was already famous in New York society. Her husband was a well-known broker on Wall Street and very wealthy. However, her first marriage was a complete failure. Perhaps the pain she suffered in her first marriage had strengthened her resolve to pursue a career in film, so that even the happiness of her second marriage could not dissuade her! This is extremely admirable.

Film Reviews

Review of "The Woman Accused" 207

— Ling He

If we are in frequent contact with American films, then it is easy to discover that the film artists of this golden country often do not give much thought to the structure of the story, but instead strive to flaunt their wealth and luxury on the screen. It can also be said that this is the characteristic of American films.

Taking this "The Woman Accused" as an example, it is not difficult to find ample confirmation. A young woman, Granda, is preparing to marry her fiancé on a ship. Her old lover obstructs her by threatening to have his gunman kill her fiancé and immediately phones the gunman. Obviously, this is illogical. Can you discuss the secret of murder over the phone? At that time, the young woman, filled with anger and hatred, struck him with a bronze statue, killing him. Afterwards, the woman told her maid the truth. The maid, disregarding the fact that she herself would be implicated, helped the woman escape. This is also very forced. I don't believe there is a loyal servant who would be so fearless of death. Later, a friend of the deceased sought justice on his behalf, proving that Granda was indeed the murderer. However, the court refused to accept the case, saying that the evidence was insufficient. This is truly making fun of the solemn law. Can the law sometimes show great mercy and allow criminals to roam free? Of course, this is because the screenwriter is too sentimental and must ensure that "lovers will always be united." But wouldn't it be more moving to have a tragic ending for this so-called happy marriage? Although it was proven that the deceased had "conspired to murder," shouldn't the one who committed "manslaughter" be sentenced to a few years in prison? As mentioned above, we are not advocating for their laws, but we want to point out their contradictions.

However, the entire picture shows that the acting skills are already pure and skilled. Director BAYARD VEILLER has used the entire plot very vividly, making us feel not at all stagnant. There are luxurious sets and beautiful cinematography. In particular, the swimming scene on the ship, the director wants to show off their wealthy lifestyle to the fullest. Of course, this is a necessary condition for Golden Country movies, but it is also their ugly exposure. As for the young woman's fiancé, using force to whip the deceased's murderer, is a very good scene. At the same time, this makes the plot take a sharp turn, which is naturally a clever technique. However, the important twists and turns are all explained through dialogue, so for viewers who do not understand English, it will inevitably reduce their interest to some extent.

Review of "Flames" 208

— Wan Shi

If we want to find an adjective to describe the passion between men and women, then "fire," FLAME, is indeed a quite suitable word. Perhaps there are better words to symbolize passion, but the film "Flames" is completely matched with fire.

The plot of the film is briefly described as follows: Two firefighters meet because they rescued a cat from a telephone pole for two young women. Who knew that these two gentlemen would fall in love with the two women at first sight and try to approach them. So, after several conversations, plus watching movies and visiting the park, one pair has already succeeded, while the other pair is half-hearted. Although the man is as passionate as fire, the woman is threatened and enticed by her manager, and she resents her lover's rudeness. Later, due to a fire in the OFFICE, the manager is grateful to the firefighter lover for saving his life, and this young couple gets married from then on.

In terms of the structure of the story, there are inevitably places that are too "coincidental," such as the sudden fire in this particular office, and the woman in the flames just happens to be waiting for her lover to come and rescue her. (Because before the lover arrived, there was already a fire truck, but they didn't save people first and only cared about putting out the fire. Of course, maybe these are all inevitable in fictional stories.) However, we don't have to have any extravagant expectations for these, because filmmakers are not necessarily realists. As for calling a fire truck for a cat, and not hesitating to drill into the flames for a bird, it is also an interpolation that is beyond reason and makes people dare not believe it. However, according to the dialogue, it tells us that it is ridiculing the fact that the firefighters' lives are not as good as a bird (because someone fell to their death for the bird), then we can only shake our heads and sigh.

The two fire scenes, before and after, are indeed very good-looking. Red fire, black smoke, women's cries for help, the roar of fire trucks, the trampling crowd, and the firefighters' desperate efforts make us viewers feel as if we are there, excited and tense. However, the director's description of so-called "familiarity" is very insufficient. If we compare it to a big fire, then obviously this "youthful fire" is not at all intense. In fact, this young couple is not passionate, and as for the insertion of jokes, there is nothing brilliant. Especially when the flames are at their highest at the end, the firefighter doesn't go to put out the fire but instead kisses the woman wildly, which is simply too unreasonable. His manager apologizes to his love rival immediately after being rescued, which is also too stiff.

Regarding the performance, there is nothing particularly good, but the relatively comical female character can give people an unforgettable impression. But if the camera were more agile, then the photography would definitely be better. In short, the performance of this film does not disappoint people too much, if we also need intense flames to stimulate our nerves.

United Star Film Company's Debut Film "Crossroads" to Begin Filming 209

— Yu Jing

In this "Film Year" of 1933, the changes in filmmaking style and the organization of film companies are rising like the wind and surging like clouds, making it very lively. It is indeed an excellent phenomenon for the domestic film industry.

The reporter would like to introduce the various emerging film companies of this year, thinking that this must be what the readers like most.

It is said that the content is very substantial, with a mine as the backdrop, which is also the first domestic film to use a mine as the backdrop. It is very worthy of our attention. The important roles in the play are played by Zheng Junli, Yuan Congmei, Tang Huaiqiu, etc. Filming has now begun.

Universal Studios Holds National Campus Beauty Contest 211

— Fu Lun

Universal Studios recently used the pages of "School Humor" and "Consciousness" magazines to hold a national campus beauty contest. Any female college student with beauty and acting talent can participate. The method is to send two photos, one profile and one front view, and a letter from the school authorities or the head of the drama department certifying the student's acting skills and vocal range. Participants must also provide details of their age, height, weight, eye color, hair color, dramatic experience, etc. The first-place winner will be given the title of "All-American Girl." She will also play the lead role in an upcoming football film, with salary and treatment based on star qualifications. In addition, she will be given a free trip to Hawaii and a weekly salary of at least one hundred US dollars during her vacation. Universal Studios has previously shot two football films, one being THE SPIREL OF NOTRE DAME ALL-AMERICAN. This special selection of the most beautiful campus beauty in the country to play the lead role in the third football film will undoubtedly have a great appeal.

An Overview of Soviet Russian Cinema (8) 212

— Written by Rudolf Mesu, Translated by Bao Han

The Soviet Russian film industry has a strong tendency to advance and is constantly planning and experimenting. However, the famous saying regarding art in the past is no longer valued in the current Soviet Russian film and theater circles. Film and theater are also not concerned about art itself. At present, Soviet Russia prioritizes education and propaganda, and art is its slave. If abstract art or artistic works can be used for propaganda, they will be used to the fullest extent. Once they lose their use, they will be discarded as if they were filth.

The Yerkov Film Studio is currently engaged in the production of DON QUIXOTE. This play is a performance costume film, and the content of the film's story is not much different from the original book. In terms of propaganda, there is no need to add or delete anything from the original book. However, the Kamerny Theatre in Moscow greatly adapted Shakespeare's HAMLET this spring in order to suit the Soviet sales market, resulting in a great discrepancy between the drama performed and the original text. For example, it was said that Hamlet's killing of Claudius had no personal intention but was an act of revolution, wanting to eliminate an evil oppressor for the poor, and so on. Furthermore, in order to emphasize this meaning, it was said that the ghost in the play was completely fabricated by Hamlet in order to deceive the army and launch a major campaign together.

The Russians are quite willing to cite historical events within a considerable scope, but they also rely on whether these events can have much relationship with the general spirit of the Five-Year Plan. For example, Shakespeare's play "Romeo and Juliet," the essence of which is extremely romantic, has no use for Soviet Russia. This idea has been repeatedly stated in Soviet Russian film and theater circles, and I myself have personally heard it said repeatedly by people in the film, theater, and book circles.

As for another famous work by Shakespeare, such as OTHELLO, a famous Soviet Russian producer once told me that the modern substitute for this play is LA COCUE MAGNIFIQUE. Although this play is an unproven Belgian work, it has actually been able to replace the masterpiece of a great master on the Russian stage.

Furthermore, "Carmen" still has a continued existence in modern Soviet Russia. I dare not say whether the plot of "Carmen" conforms to the spirit of the Five-Year Plan. Furthermore, the modern production of Bizet's opera has not undergone any modifications. We have no way of determining the reason for its success or failure, so we can only say that "Carmen" and others are like the works of Hal Roach, accidentally mixed in the film industry and have become firmly established over the years. Judging from the daily actions of Carmen and Hal Roach, my words are also quite appropriate. (The End)
